------------------------------------
Pass a value from a main form to a subform control as a default value - Microsoft Community

stanmitchell5342 say:

Pass a value from a main form to a subform control as a default value

Hello everyone!  I have frmSponsorEntry and subfrmDocumentEntry, which populate tblSponsors and tblDocuments respectively.  In frmSponsorEntry, I have a combo box cmbSponsorName with field [State] as Column 0.  I would like to have subfrmDocumentEntry's control cmbDocumentState display the value of frmSponsorEntry.cmbSponsorName column 0.

I've tried placing this in the Default Value of subfrmDocumentEntry.cmbDocumentState but nothing displays when I change focus from the main form to the subform.

=[frmSponsorEntry]![cmbSponsorName].[Column](0)

99% of the time, the document's state will be the same as the sponsor's state but I need to allow for the possibility that they are not.  I think the issue may be related to the fact that there are no records in tblDocuments related to the sponsor until something changes in the subform.  If it helps, cmbDocumentState is the first control on subfrmDocumentEntry.  Perhaps some sort of On Focus event is needed?

Thanks in advance!

stanmitchell5342 say:

Actually, I just solved it.  I added an Event on Got Focus for subfrmDocumentEntry.DocumentState:

Private Sub cmbDocumentState_GotFocus()

 Me.cmbDocumentState = Me.Parent.cmbSponsorName.Column(0)

End Sub

That did exactly what I wanted.  I tab down the main form, when I tab to the subform, subfrmDocumentState is the first stop and it populated instantly.  I'm sure there's an easier way but using VBA made sense to me.

a. user say:

Hi,

As you are unable to sign in to your Email account due to the security code which you are not able to receive on your new phone number, I suggest you to select the option of sending the security code to your alternative Email account which you have added/provided for security purpose of this Email account. The security code shall be sent to your alternative Email account. You may use this security code to sign into your Email account. After signing in to your Email account, you may change or remove your phone number.

Hope this information is helpful. For any further information, feel free to contact us.

Thank you.

a. user say:

Hi,

As you are unable to find the option to receive the security code using Email account, I suggest you to try resetting the password of your Email account and check. Follow the steps provided below.

  1. Click on https://outlook.live.com/

  2. Click on Forgot my password.

  3. Select I Forgot my password option and click Next button.

  4. Enter your Email address and verification alphanumeric code you see in the image and click Next button.

  5. Select Email address option and follow the on screen instruction.

After successfully changing your Email account password, you may access your Security Information page and change the phone number.

Hope it helps. Do let us know the status of the issue. For any further information, feel free to contact us.

Thank you.

Windows 10 - Upgrading from W7 Home Pro - Microsoft Community

paulwhiteman say:

Windows 10 - Upgrading from W7 Home Pro

Ok, so let's pretend I'm a total idiot.  Not hard to do, just ask my daughter...

In the past, when installing or upgrading an OS, I would have to reinstall everything.  Being that I'm a photographer and have a host of apps and programs, this could prove to be a daunting task.  So, I ask:  Will I have to reinstall everything?

Secondly, and perhaps more importantly, the laptop I use is a "tower replacement" Toshiba Qosmio.  (It's a "tower replacement" because it's a massive laptop with multiple HDDs and a host of features usually reserved for towers)

My question is this:  In the "10 Things to do to install the Windows 10 Upgrade" thread, it is suggested that you remove/disable any secondary or tertiary hard drives.  Being that I can't exactly crack open my laptop and just disconnect/remove the second drive - 

Is it absolutely necessary to do this before I upgrade to Windows 10?

Finally, is this upgrade going to disable Office 2010?

mel77084 say:

Ok, Paul, let's just say perhaps not yet fully informed, but working on it.

First, what is your recovery plan that you will implement when (not if) your hard drive (the one that your OS and all your installed programs are on) fails? They all do, you know ... we just don't yet know when.

I mention that because after you upgrade to Windows 10, you might find that one or more of your special programs for photography might not work correctly yet ... you might need to wait for a newer version that's not out yet ... and, so, you might need to go back, for a while, to Windows 7, in order to handle your photographic work.

See the similarity of those two scenarios? What you will need in either case is a disk image type of file, saved on a Windows 7 and installed programs). That restoration will require booting to a rescue CD, which is made by the same disk imaging program, of which there are several, some free for personal use, and some not free, but inexpensive.

Imagining that you are a prudent business person, I fully expect that you you are already making use of such a program to protect your system; however, I will say that every day we see many examples of those who put it off until it's too late, and then cry for help.

Data files have no place in the OS partition, even though the installed program that produces the data exists there. Example: An accounting program produces data files that should be in a separate data partition, for convenience of backup, and so that, if you decide after a month or two, to return to your old OS and installed programs, the accounting data files are undisturbed and ready to be used, modified, etc. 

Similarly, such files as downloaded program installers, etc, should be in a separate partition ... they take up a lot of space, and do no good sitting in the OS partition.

One should refrain from having folders of files on the desktop. They should be in their appropriate places, with desktop shortcuts to them, if convenience dictates.

Once the OS partition is pared down to only the OS and the installed programs, it is time to make the image of the partition, and store it on another hard drive. The frequency of system changes should dictate how often images are made, and the last 2 or 3 should be saved. If you are not practicing that now, you'll surely want to start it before beginning the Windows 10 upgrade, in case anything goes wrong, even though Windows 10 will be quite effective in undoing the changes to your system in the event of the installation failing.

Now, to answer your question about needing to reinstall your programs after upgrading to Windows 10: No, not if you in order to have a fresh start ... some strongly prefer doing that, even with all the extra work of reinstalling programs.

As to the question about disconnecting other drives, you shouldn't need to do that ... it was listed as possibly desirable for ones who plan to do a clean install, and might get confused about which drive is which. In an upgrade, the installation is automatically into the partition of the OS that is being upgraded.

3rd party security programs ... should be uninstalled, cleanly, which in some cases, requires getting the special uninstaller from the provider of the security program.  Some have said, "oh, I deactivated it", but found that it still hampered the installation of Windows 10. That said, several of the 3rd party programs are compatible now, but it's safer to finish the upgrade before trying one ... and I would wait for the provider to specify that theirs is compatible.  It's entirely possible for one that seems to work ok to cause problems that might get blamed incorrectly on the OS.

windows_insider_program,
windows_insider_preview,
install,_upgrade,_and_activate,
pc,

william wielders say:

It's a driver thing. If you disable audio it will be good and the install goes on. That was the case in my situation. Once Windows 10 build 9926 is installed enable audio again to install it. Or leave it off if it's not compatible.

In VMware Windows 10 build 9926 will install audio but with the option off in VMware you won't hear sound. After you enable it you will hear sounds from Windows 10 ;)

ps. If disabling audio in VMware does not do the trick, disable temp. other hardware such as the NIC and enable it again in VMware options after Windows 10 is successfully installed.

bolean say: Just wait! "Getting Ready" screen took me 10 (ten] hours!!!

william wielders say:

With my fix, it took me 12 minutes :)

Is anyone working on Microsoft Publisher ? It isn't showing - Microsoft Community

carolhaaz say:

Is anyone working on Microsoft Publisher ? It isn't showing clip art

I need to be able to use publisher and none of the clipart is working

davidf2 say:

Sorry, but it looks like MSFT has decided that Publisher users no longer want or need the clipart collection. <sigh>

They have been phasing out clipart support along with Publisher templates for some years now.  If you go to the Templates web page there is no mention of Publisher templates at all anymore. There used to be hundreds.

Reference: Clip Art on Office Online has been retired (2007 & 2010): https://support.office.com/en-us/article/clip-art-on-office-online-has-been-retired-4b0bba44-1d84-4a5e-8822-466769a244a2?ui=en-US&rs=en-US&ad=US

- In Office 2007 and Office 2010, there's no longer an online clip art library.

It is probably futile but at the bottom of that page you will find an invitation: "if an online clip art library is a feature you'd like to see brought back to Office, please send us your feedback."

Who knows, if enough users actually do send some feedback...

By the way, those people using older versions of Publisher had local built in clipart collections and you should still be able to access them. I am sorry, I don't remember when MSFT moved everything to the cloud, but I thought that Pub 2007 came with a clipart gallery. 

[Edit] Here is a good reference discussion for Pub 2007 users from five years ago. I had to laugh because I had forgotten some/a lot of what we learned back then. I don't know if the methods or workarounds still work or not.

Reference: Clip Art in Publisher Not Working: http://answers.microsoft.com/en-us/office/forum/office_2007-publish/clip-art-in-publisher-not-working/25c54df1-b8d4-4a46-8ec8-648ee4b61080

DavidF

roger haight msft say:

Several days ago, in late March, the Office team mistakenly turned off the ability to search online for clip art from Office 2010/2007. That's the cause of what you experienced, CarolHaaz. We're very sorry. This problem was fixed late yesterday afternoon, April 5. Online search results for clip art in Office are working again. 

DavidF2: Just to clarify: The article you found (https://support.office.com/en-us/article/clip-art-on-office-online-has-been-retired-4b0bba44-1d84-4a5e-8822-466769a244a2) is describing a different case that is permanent: Back when Office 2010 was first released, there were two dedicated sources of licensed clip art in Office: (1) the local clip art collection, which you mentioned, and (2) an online library of clip art on the Office.com web site. That online library of clip art is no longer available. That's what the "Clip art in Office Online" article is referring to. 
Since the online clip art library was retired a few years ago, Office let you search the web for clip art -- you do this by checking the "Include Bing content" box in the clip art dialog -- as you well know. That's the feature that's been broken for several days and was fixed yesterday. 

davidf2 say:

Thanks for the update.

Will the user have to 'repair' or 'update' Publisher or the OS in order to regain this functionality or was the 'cloud' fixed and no action is needed by the user?

DavidF
